**SCP-3211:** There is No Canon
**Author:** [[*user Croquembouche]]

Hidden behind your phone or computer screen, you're usually safe from antimemetic SCPs.
But 3211? No no no. 3211 is different.

You'll only get to read this one once. After the timer has finished and you've read the final version of the article, check the Discussion for instructions on how to reset it.

var anomalies = [];
for(let a = 0; a < anomalyDict.length; a++) {
    anomalies[a] = [

    	constant[3],
    	constant[0],

var assign = function(name, value) {
  console.log("Saving " + value + " to " + name);
  storage.setItem(name, value);
  Cookies.set(name, value, {
    expires: 356
  });
  $("#anomalyCookie").text(" Current: " + anomaly);
  $("#otherCookies").text(" Current: seen " + Cookies.get("seen") + ", timer " + Cookies.get("timerExpiresAt"));
};

var decrypt = function(decryptee) {
  console.log("Decrypting...");
  return decryptee.replace(/[a-zA-Z]/g, function (c) {
    return String.fromCharCode((c <= "Z" ? 90 : 122) >= (c = c.charCodeAt(0) + 13) ? c : c - 26);
  });
};

var resetCookie = function(cookie) {
    console.log("Cleared localStorage: " + cookie + " " + storage.getItem(cookie));
  storage.removeItem(cookie);
  console.log("Cleared cookie: " + cookie + " " + Cookies.get(cookie));
  Cookies.remove(cookie);
};

var resetCookies = function(reloadPageAfter) {
    console.log("Resetting cookies...");
  resetCookie("anomaly");
  resetCookie("seen");
  resetCookie("timerExpiresAt");
    if(reloadPageAfter) {
    resetCookie("seenNew");
    javascript: history.go(0);
    }
};

var str_pad_left = function(string, pad, length) {
  return (new Array(length + 1).join(pad) + string).slice(-length);
};

// If anyone knows how to make footnotes appear on mouseover please let me know because this doesn't work
var hoverdiv = function(e) {
  var divid = "hovertip";
  var left = 0; //e.clientX + "px";
  var top = (e.clientY + 10) + "px";
  var div = document.getElementById(divid);
  div.style.left = left;
  div.style.top = top;
  $("#" + divid).toggle();
  console.log("Footnote activated");
  return false;
};

// LocalStorage does not work with Safari incognito mode
var canUseLocalStorage = (function() {
  try {
    localStorage.getItem("test");
    return true;
  } catch (e) {
    return false;
  }
})();

var storage = canUseLocalStorage ? {
  getItem: function (key) {
    return localStorage.getItem(key);
  },
  setItem: function (key, value) {
    localStorage.setItem(key, value);
  },
  removeItem: function (key) {
    localStorage.removeItem(key);
  }
} : {
  getItem: function () {
    return null;
  },
  setItem: function () {},
  removeItem: function () {}
};

var currentSection = "warning";
var decryptedAnomaly = "<p>No anomaly was decrypted</p>";
var read = false;
var anomaly;

// 1. SPLASH - determine iteration and wait for user input. All code here is executed immediately.
// Apparently jQuery events need to go in here too. I miss Angular
$(document).ready(function () {
  console.log("%cSCP-2MIN is ready", "font-size:20px;");
  // first, check if they've already seen the new entries
  if(Cookies.get("seenNew") || storage.getItem("seenNew")) {
  	//proceed with default behaviour
  	console.log("User has seen the updated version at least once");
  	assign("seenNew", true);
  } else {
  	// force a reset
  	console.log("User has not seen the updated version. Resetting");
  	assign("seenNew", true);
  	resetCookies(false);
  }
  
  // Attempt to detect what iteration the reader previously viewed
  if (Cookies.get("anomaly")) {
    anomaly = Cookies.get("anomaly");
    console.log("Previous anomaly " + anomaly + " detected from cookie");
  } else if (storage.getItem("anomaly")) {
    anomaly = storage.getItem("anomaly");
    console.log("Previous anomaly " + anomaly + " detected from storage");
  } else {
    // Looks like the reader is a SCP-2MIN virgin, or is at least pretending to be.
    // Pick a random iteration from the list
    anomaly = Math.floor(Math.random() * (anomalies.length));
    console.log("Initialising anomaly");
  }
  anomaly = parseInt(anomaly);
  console.log("Viewing " + anomaly);
  assign("anomaly", anomaly);
  // iteration now contains the entire body of an anomaly, but still encrypted. Decrypt it during Loading.
  // Await user input.

  // Now let's define some functions while we wait.

  // Ooo super secret
  $("span[type='authorise']").on("click", function () {
    $("#BUTTONS").removeClass("HIDDEN");
  });

  // Reset and forget
  $("#reset").on("click", true, resetCookies);

  // Manually stop the anomaly timer
  $("#stopTimer").on("click", function () {
    clearInterval(window.clock);
    console.log("Timer was stopped.");
    delete window.clock;
  });

  // Whether or not to ignore the seen cookie
  $("#ignoreSeen").on("click", function () {
    assign("seen", false);
  });

  // Manually adjust the iteration value
  $(".anomalySelector").on("click", function () {
    anomaly = $(this).text();
    console.log("Anomaly manually set to " + anomaly);
    assign("anomaly", anomaly);
  });

  // 2. LOADING - provide an additional splash screen while we decrypt the selected iteration.
  $("#proceed").on("click", function () {
    console.log("Proceed was clicked");
    // Most important thing first - let's check whether or not the user is using incognito mode.
    // tretter says nay! let's not do this
    // next most important thing then is to detect whether or not the reader has already read scp-2min
    // we do this by checking for SEEN

    // switch to loading
    $("#LOADING").removeClass("HIDDEN");
    $("#WARNING").addClass("HIDDEN");
    currentSection = "loading";
    console.log("Now in section Loading");

    // work out whether or not we need to skip ahead to Review
    var destSection;
    if (Cookies.get("seen")) {
      //seen = Cookies.get("seen");
      console.log("Cookie claims already seen");
      assign("seen", true);
      destSection = "review";
    } else if (storage.getItem("seen")) {
      //seen = storage.getItem("seen");
      console.log("Storage claims already seen");
      destSection = "review";
      assign("seen", true);
    } else {
      // We do not need to skip ahead to Review
      destSection = "anomaly";
      decryptedAnomaly = decrypt(anomalies[anomaly]);
      $("#anomalyContent").html(decryptedAnomaly);
    }
    // Now we have a little spare time during the Loading phase to initialise the stuff that Anomaly depends on (because anomaly didn't exist on load)
    // Proceed to the next section after 1.2 seconds
    setTimeout(nextSection, 1200, destSection, currentSection);

    // Handles opening and closing of collapsibles. Copied straight from WIKIDOT.combined.js with a slight modification to target specific collapsibles.
    $("div.collapsible-block a.collapsible-block-link").on("click", function () {
      var c = $("div.collapsible-block." + $(this).attr("target"));
      var activated_c = $(this).parents("div.collapsible-block");
      c.each(function (index) {
        var d = $(this);
        if (activated_c.find(".collapsible-block-folded").css("display") == "block") {
          d.find(".collapsible-block-folded").hide();
          var e = d.find(".collapsible-block-unfolded");
          e.find(".collapsible-block-content").hide();
          e.show();
          e.find(".collapsible-block-content").fadeIn("fast");
        } else {
          d.find(".collapsible-block-unfolded").hide();
          d.find(".collapsible-block-folded").show();
        }
      });
    });

    // Click "read" if you've read the document and want the timer to end
    $("span.read").on("click", function () {
      read = true;
    });
  });
});

var nextSection = function (next, from) {
  // move onto the next section
  // this will either take us from Loading to Anomaly, or from Anomaly to Review, or from Loading to Review
  // prepare for each case in this order
  switch (next) {
    case "anomaly":
      // The only possible way to be switching to anomaly is from loading, so we need to render anomaly and start the timer, no questions asked
      currentSection = "anomaly";
      console.log("Now in section Anomaly");

      // Set anomaly content and display it // already set
      $("#ANOMALY").removeClass("HIDDEN");
      $("#LOADING").addClass("HIDDEN");

      // Set the timer cookie to maintain 30 seconds even if user navigates away, because I am a dick
      var expiry;
      var secondsRemaining;
      if (Cookies.get("timerExpiresAt")) {
        // timerIsRunning is set, the user is here for the second time. just leave it how it is
        console.log("Previous viewing session detected! Resuming previous timer.");
        expiry = new Date(Cookies.get("timerExpiresAt"));
        secondsRemaining = Math.floor((expiry.getTime() - new Date().getTime()) / 1000);
      } else if (storage.getItem("timerExpiresAt")) {
        console.log("Previous viewing session detected! Resuming previous timer.");
        expiry = new Date(storage.getItem("timerExpiresAt"));
        secondsRemaining = Math.floor((expiry.getTime() - new Date().getTime()) / 1000);
      } else {
        // timerIsRunning is not set, user is genuine
        expiry = new Date(Date.now() + readTime * 1000); // this is the exact date and time in 30 seconds. Increased a little for buffer
        //Cookies.set("timerIsRunning", true, {expires: expiry}); // cookie should expire in 30 seconds - now we check either for 30 default seconds, or not cookie
        assign("timerExpiresAt", expiry);
        secondsRemaining = readTime;
      }

      // Run the timer loop
      //var secondsRemaining = readTime;
      var timer = $("p.timer");
      window.clock = setInterval(function () {
        if (secondsRemaining === 0 || secondsRemaining < 0) {
          clearInterval(clock);
          nextSection("review", currentSection);
          // timerIsRunning cookie will have cleared itself by now
          storage.removeItem("timerExpiresAt");
          Cookies.remove("timerExpiresAt");
        } else {
          if (read && secondsRemaining > 5) {
            secondsRemaining = 6
          }
          var frac = secondsRemaining / readTime;
          console.log("%c" + secondsRemaining + "s", "color: rgba(" + (255 - Math.ceil((frac) * 255)) + "," + Math.ceil((frac) * 255) + ",0,1); font-size:15px;"); // Yeah I'm a cool kid
          secondsRemaining--;

          var minutes = Math.floor(secondsRemaining / 60);
          var seconds = secondsRemaining - minutes * 60;
          timer.text(str_pad_left(minutes, "0", 2) + ":" + str_pad_left(seconds, "0", 2));
        }
      }, 1000);
      break;

    case "review":
      // This can happen either by Loading detecting a seen cookie, or by Anomaly progressing normally
      currentSection = "review";
      console.log("Now in section Review");
      $("#REVIEW").removeClass("HIDDEN");
      if (from == "anomaly") {
        $("#ANOMALY").addClass("HIDDEN");
      } else if (from == "loading") {
        $("#LOADING").addClass("HIDDEN");
      } else {
        console.log("ERROR: coming into review from " + from);
      }
      // The document has been SEEN, so we must set the SEEN cookie
      assign("seen", true);
      break;

    default:
      throw "Bad case, this shouldn't happen";
  };
};
</script>

<DIV CLASS="SECTION HIDDEN" ID="REVIEW">
  <blockquote class='timer'><p><b>Memetic detectors indicate that you were first exposed to this file more than 6 minutes ago. You are now considered post-3211. If you can still perceive the documentation as you originally recall it, please consult a researcher assigned to SCP-3211 immediately.</b></p></blockquote><div class='scp-image-block block-right' style='width: 300px;'><img src='http://scp-wiki.wdfiles.com/local--files/scp-3211/imgmissing.png' style='width: 300px;' alt='scp.jpg' class='image'><div class='scp-image-caption' style='width: 300px;'><p>There is no photographic evidence of SCP-3211.</p></div></div><p><b>Item #:</b> SCP-3211</p><p><b>Object Class:</b> Euclid</p><p><b>Special Containment Procedures:</b> To reduce unnecessary exposure to SCP-3211, a warning message is to be placed at the start of this document. Level 4 authorisation must be required to proceed. No information regarding SCP-3211 is to be present in any resources not exclusively available to researchers assigned to SCP-3211, including the warning message.</p><p>Except in the event of an emergency necessitating knowledge of SCP-3211, no more than 3 members of the O5 council and 10% of the population of any individual Site are to have been exposed to information regarding SCP-3211 other than its existence.</p><p>SCP-3211 is to be kept in a standard non-humanoid containment chamber. Access is to be limited to tests only.</p><p><b>Description:</b> SCP-3211 is an unknown object, entity or concept.</p><p>SCP-3211 exhibits a slow-acting but potent perception-altering effect. During the first 6 minutes of exposure to SCP-3211, subjects are able to observe and record SCP-3211 without issue. Once 6 minutes have passed, subjects will immediately and permanently be unable to perceive any direct information associated with SCP-3211, or observe SCP-3211 itself. This effectively quarantines information about SCP-3211 to only those who have been exposed to it for less than 6 minutes.</p><p>For the purposes of this document, subjects who have already been exposed to SCP-3211 for at least 6 minutes will be described as <b>post-3211</b> and those who have been exposed to it for less than 6 minutes will be described as <b>pre-3211</b>.</p><p>Post-3211 subjects are consistently adamant that they are able to perfectly remember its nature despite being unable to take in new information about it. However, it quickly becomes apparent that each post-3211 subject reports a different description for SCP-3211. A selection of such descriptions, in chronological order of their being reported, is provided below.</p><p><ul><li>████-brand microwave oven</li><li><i>Homo sapiens</i>, Czech female, named 'Nerozumím'</li><li>Porcelain mug printed with imagery from █████████ franchise, empty</li><li>Red cube, perfectly smooth, 12 cm on all sides</li><li><i>Columba livia domestica</i> (common pigeon) corpse, early stages of decomposition</li><li>The colour 'puce'</li><li>Clay vase, presumably ancient</li><li>DVD boxset of the television series 'Friends', missing one disc from season 3</li><li>A small plastic badge imprinted with the number '3211'</li></ul></p><p>Of note is that descriptions of the object vary only between post-3211 subjects. Observations indicate that pre-3211 subjects consistently agree on the nature of SCP-3211. However, once these subjects pass the 6-minute threshold, they will disagree on what it is. This also applies to documentation: personnel viewing this document universally report that it describes something else before it changes after 6 minutes. See Experiment Logs 3211-01 and -02 for more details.</p><p>Note that post-3211 subjects reporting unique descriptions is not universal — in several cases, the same description has been reported more than once.</p><p>The fact that those who have been exposed to SCP-3211 are able to read the list above suggests that none of those descriptions are what SCP-3211 truly is. Several theories have been suggested:</p><p><ul><li>That none of the descriptions are true, and that the real SCP-3211 has yet to be seen.</li><li>That none of the descriptions are true, and that the real SCP-3211 will reveal itself to someone 'worthy'.</li><li>That one of the above descriptions is true, and the rest are false.</li><li>That all of the above descriptions are true, and that SCP-3211 is somehow several objects located in the same conceptual space.</li></ul></p><p>The mechanism through which SCP-3211 propagates this effect is currently unknown, though the current theory proposes that after the 6-minute threshold, SCP-3211 'injects' false memories over the original perception.</p><p>Amnestics have proven to be effective on post-3211 subjects. They will forget SCP-3211 as expected, and upon re-exposure may perceive it as something new. A method of amnesticating only the false memories has not yet been found.</p><p><b>Addendum 3211-A:</b> Experiment Logs 3211-01 and 3211-02</p><p><div class='collapsible-block 2min-b'><div class='collapsible-block-folded' style='display: block;'><a class='collapsible-block-link' target='2min-b'>► Experiment Log 3211-01</a></div><div class='collapsible-block-unfolded' style='display: none;'><div class='collapsible-block-unfolded-link'><a class='collapsible-block-link' target='2min-b'>▼ Experiment Log 3211-01</a></div><div class='collapsible-block-content' style='display: block;'><blockquote><p style='text-align: center;'><b>EXPERIMENT LOG 3211-01</b></p><hr><p>The purpose of this experiment was to establish a firsthand written description of SCP-3211 and then compare this description with another observer.</p><p>D-68134 was given a pencil, clipboard and a single sheet of paper. He was instructed to enter the containment cell and produce a written description of its contents.</p><hr><p><b>[</b>-0:10<b>]</b> D-68134 enters the containment chamber with his eyes closed.</p><p><b>[</b>0:00<b>]</b> D-68134 is instructed to open his eyes.</p><p><b>[</b>0:08<b>]</b> D-68134 begins writing a description of SCP-3211.</p><p><b>[</b>6:04<b>]</b> D-68134 expresses surprise that he can no longer perceive SCP-3211. He expresses anger at not being able to read what he has written.</p><p><b>[</b>6:25<b>]</b> D-68134 is instructed to leave the containment chamber.</p><hr><p>The description produced by D-68134 was retained as Document 3211-01.</p></blockquote></div></div></div></p><p><div class='collapsible-block 2min-d'><div class='collapsible-block-folded' style='display:block'><a class='collapsible-block-link' target='2min-d'>► Experiment Log 3211-02</a></div><div class='collapsible-block-unfolded' style='display:none'><div class='collapsible-block-unfolded-link'><a class='collapsible-block-link' target='2min-d'>▼ Experiment Log 3211-02</a></div><div class='collapsible-block-content' style='display:block'><blockquote><p style='text-align:center'><b>EXPERIMENT LOG 3211-02</b></p><hr><p>The purpose of this experiment was to compare the written description from Experiment 3211-01 with another observer.</p><p>D-8834 is provided with Document 3211-01 and instructed not to read it.</p><hr><p><b>[</b>-0:10<b>]</b> D-8834 enters the containment chamber with her eyes closed.</p><p><b>[</b>0:00<b>]</b> D-8834 is instructed to open her eyes and compare the object in the room to the description on Document 3211-01.</p><p><b>[</b>1:18<b>]</b> D-8834 confirms that the SCP-3211 matches the written description.</p><p><b>[</b>5:45<b>]</b> D-8834 is asked to close her eyes.</p><p><b>[</b>6:15<b>]</b> D-8834 is asked to compare the object to the written description again, from memory.</p><p><b>[</b>6:34<b>]</b> D-8834 confirms that Document 3211-01 describes a completely different object to SCP-3211.</p><p><b>[</b>6:44<b>]</b> D-8834 is asked to open her eyes. She reports that she is neither able to perceive the object nor read Document 3211-01.</p></blockquote></div></div></div></p><p><div class='collapsible-block 2min-c'><div class='collapsible-block-folded' style='display: block;'><a class='collapsible-block-link' target='2min-c'>► Document 3211-01</a></div><div class='collapsible-block-unfolded' style='display: none;'><div class='collapsible-block-unfolded-link'><a class='collapsible-block-link' target='2min-c'>▼ Document 3211-01</a></div><div class='collapsible-block-content' style='display: block;'><p>The following is a copy of Document 3211-01, the text produced by D-68134 during Experiment 3211-01.</p><blockquote><p>The containment chamber is empty. There's nothing to describe. I don't understand why I have to write about an empty room.</p></blockquote></div></div></div></p><p><b>Addendum 3211-B:</b> Empirical data</p><p>As an attempt to determine the true nature of SCP-3211, a collection of data has been recorded from SCP-3211 and is listed below. This data has been recorded only by pre-3211 researchers, but it is currently unknown whether the readings are accurate, or if the reader perceives them to match their current perception of SCP-3211.</p><p><table class='wiki-content-table'><tr><th>Data type</th><th>Observation</th></tr><tr><td>Full-spectrum spectrophotometry</td><td>SCP-3211 displays absorbances and transmittances in the visible spectrum consistent with standard background reading</td></tr><tr><td>Mass</td><td>Mass balance placed underneath the location of SCP-3211 did not detect any weight</td></tr><tr><td>Hume measurement</td><td>SCP-3211 has a Hume reading consistent with baseline reality</td></tr><tr><td>Magnetism</td><td>SCP-3211 is not magnetic</td></tr><tr><td>Visual observation by D-9981</td><td>SCP-3211 is not visually present</td></tr><tr><td>Physical observation by D-9981</td><td>No response. D-9981 did not feel anything at SCP-3211's location</td></tr><tr><td>Response to basic questioning by D-9981</td><td>No response</td></tr><tr><td>Type-Kappa memetic sentience detector</td><td>Negative response</td></tr></table></p><p><b>Incident Log 3211-C:</b> On 2016-03-31, a researcher who was not assigned to SCP-3211, Dr. Jason Greaves, took a Class-Y mnestic<sup class='footnoteref'><a id='footnoteref-1' class='footnoteref'  onmouseover='hoverdiv(event)' onmouseout='hoverdiv(event)'>1</a></sup> without authorisation and entered the containment chamber. Personnel reported being unable to perceive Dr. Greaves until his unconscious body was noted to 'spontaneously appear' several hours later. Dr. Greaves returned to full health with medical care, but did not retain any details of his encounter with SCP-3211, claiming only that he 'wasted his time in an empty cell'.</p><p>Dr. Greaves recorded a series of audio logs detailing his thought process during his encounter. However, the content of these logs propagate the infohazardous effect, and are effectively devoid of information. Their transcriptions are preserved below for posterity.</p><p>Dr. Greaves has been severely reprimanded for not following standard testing procedure.</p><p><div class='collapsible-block 2min-f'><div class='collapsible-block-folded' style='display: block; margin-bottom: 200px;'><a class='collapsible-block-link' target='2min-f'>► Audio Log of Incident 3211-F</a></div><div class='collapsible-block-unfolded' style='display: none;'><div class='collapsible-block-unfolded-link'><a class='collapsible-block-link' target='2min-f'>▼ Audio Log of Incident 3211-F</a></div><div class='collapsible-block-content' style='display: block;'><blockquote><p>Dr. Jason Greaves, SCP-3211, experiment log... one?</p><p>If you're hearing this and if, like me, you're souped-up on some heavy-ass mnestics, then you and me both know for sure that SCP-3211 does not exist. Why it's trying so hard to hide that from us, we'll never know. But, if you're not high as hell on Class Y, then in less than 6 minutes you'll only remember me just rambling on about some random thing sat in a containment chamber.</p><p>And of course, when that happens, all these logs will say is that there's nothing in the containment chamber at all.</p><p>What I'm trying to do is work out exactly what SCP-3211 is, how it works, and why it's trying so hard to hide. What does it want?</p><p>No matter what I tried and who I spoke to, I couldn't get this test authorised. But it needs to be done. So I've taken a small dose of Class Y mnestics and I'm doing this myself. I only have a couple of hours before the Class Y stops helping me remember things and starts making me forget things, so I'd better get started.</p></blockquote><blockquote><p>I've noticed something of a pattern emerging.</p><p>Most people who walk into 3211's cell will perceive the cell to be completely empty. Like, I can clearly see that there is nothing here.</p><p>There is nothing in the containment cell. SCP-3211 does not exist.</p><p>It seems to me like Foundation personnel — researchers and the like — will perceive the containment cell to be completely empty. People who are already familiar with nothing, who are <i>expecting</i> nothing, will see nothing in the containment chamber, because it is empty.</p><p>But a D-Class, for example, who is not familiar with the anomalous, will remember the containment cell being empty, just the same.</p><p>It looks like SCP-3211 does not exist at all. But I still don't understand why, if SCP-3211 does not exist, I insist on trying to prove that it does. SCP-3211 does not exist.</p><p>My head feels... foggy. I don't know if it's the SCP or the mnestics starting to wear off. I actually don't know how long Class Y lasts.</p></blockquote><blockquote><p>I think I've narrowed it down to three... stages. That seems to be the right word.</p><p>So, the first stage is what you see when you walk into the cell for the first time; what SCP-3211 really is. It's nothing. Obviously, as soon as my mnestics wear off, I'll forget that. And so will you. I assume you've taken mnestics.</p><p>The second stage is whatever memory SCP-3211 injects over itself when you've seen it for more than 6 minutes. Last time I saw it, I remembered seeing... my son. Who would be six. That was the second perception for me.</p><p>The third stage is that you can't perceive it at all. Its disguise is complete and it's hidden from you.</p><p>I think I know why it wants to hide. I just... need to put the words into a sentence.</p><p>It's getting hard to think. My thoughts feel like walking through ketchup.</p></blockquote><blockquote><p>Oh God, my head is killing me.</p><p>I'm certain it's the mnestics. Class Z literally kills you when you take it, because the effect is permanent. Class Y won't kill you... I hope? I, uh... might have majorly fucked up by doing this.</p><p>It's really weird seeing all the things you can't usually remember. There's bugs everywhere, covering every surface. The containment cell is empty. There are no bugs.</p><p>I need to sleep. I just want to sleep.</p></blockquote><blockquote><p>The floor is so much more comfortable than standing.</p><p>It's getting hard to breathe. I don't know if that's my lungs closing up, or if it's just the... if it's just me forgetting <i>how</i>. At least I haven't forgotten what it was the first time I saw it.</p><p>But I know for sure why SCP-3211 wants to disguise so avidly. It's right there, just in front of you. I'm surprised no one has seen it yet.</p><p>It's just... it's just that it's not really... it's not really there. It does not exist.</p></blockquote><blockquote><p>I don't know how to take mnestics, dammit. I only make them. I know how they're... how they're...</p><p>I need to sleep.</p><p>I am alone in this room. The containment cell is empty. Just... just make me forget already.</p><p>I know that it does not exist... why don't... why can't... why did you have to show him to me?</p><p>Why did you have to take him away again?</p><p>I don't think I'm going to survive.</p><p>Why hasn't anyone come to get me?</p></blockquote><p>It is assumed that Dr. Greaves fell unconscious at this point. The remainder of the logs are mostly silent up to the point where a member of security staff noticed Dr. Greaves on closed-circuit monitoring several minutes later and called for help.</p></div></div></div></p><p><div class='footnotes-footer'><div class='title'>Footnotes</div><div class='footnote-footer' id='footnote-1'><a>1</a>. ''Mnestics, as opposed to the more common amnestics, generally aid in the retention of memories and the prevention of their modification even in the face of anomalies that seek to disrupt this...'' – Excerpt from <i>An Introduction to Antimemetic Counter-Measures</i>, <a href='http://www.scp-wiki.net/we-need-to-talk-about-fifty-five' target='_top'>Marion Wheeler</a></div></div></p>
</DIV>
